<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7bc82ec8-86d6-4ac6-8cc0-710bc95b666a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer1614543002370038717">A missing girl on a journey of revenge. A <i>Serial</i>―like podcast following the clues she's left behind. And an ending you won't be able to stop talking about.<br/><br/>Sadie hasn't had an easy life.   <span id="freeText1614543002370038717" style="display:none">A missing girl on a journey of revenge. A <i>Serial</i>―like podcast following the clues she's left behind. And an ending you won't be able to stop talking about.<br /><br />Sadie hasn't had an easy life. Growing up on her own, she's been raising her sister Mattie in an isolated small town, trying her best to provide a normal life and keep their heads above water.<br /><br />But when Mattie is found dead, Sadie's entire world crumbles. After a somewhat botched police investigation, Sadie is determined to bring her sister's killer to justice and hits the road following a few meager clues to find him.<br /><br />When West McCray―a radio personality working on a segment about small, forgotten towns in America―overhears Sadie's story at a local gas station, he becomes obsessed with finding the missing girl. He starts his own podcast as he tracks Sadie's journey, trying to figure out what happened, hoping to find her before it's too late.<br /><br />Courtney Summers has written the breakout book of her career. Sadie is propulsive and harrowing and will keep you riveted until the last page.</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    As far as I know there won’t be a second book. Personally, I think Sadie died but I like that it’s left ambiguous for two reasons 1) it’s more hopeful<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    As far as I know there won’t be a second book. Personally, I think Sadie died but I like that it’s left ambiguous for two reasons 1) it’s more hopeful that way; 2) it’s more true to life that things are left messy with loose ends and unresolved questions. Like many real crimes it’s a case of we’ll probably just never know. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

</script>    </div>

<div id="review_2464447205" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2464447205" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2464447205?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2464447205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12698826081088288756"><em>Sadie</em> splintered in my heart, and I’m sure the author meant it to. I finished it, shivering with a chill inside me that nothing could possibly drive away. It’s been days and I still can’t swallow past the unaccountable lump in my throat. But I guess that’s just it—all that is harder to read, proves much slower to heal.<br/><br/><em>
  <u>
    So, what's this book about?
  </u>
</em><br/><br/>Nineteen-years-old Sadie has raised her little sister, thirteen-years-old Mattie, since she was born to Claire, their drug-addicted absent mo</span>
  <span id="freeText12698826081088288756" style="display:none"><em>Sadie</em> splintered in my heart, and I’m sure the author meant it to. I finished it, shivering with a chill inside me that nothing could possibly drive away. It’s been days and I still can’t swallow past the unaccountable lump in my throat. But I guess that’s just it—all that is harder to read, proves much slower to heal.<br /><br /><em>
  <u>
    So, what's this book about?
  </u>
</em><br /><br />Nineteen-years-old Sadie has raised her little sister, thirteen-years-old Mattie, since she was born to Claire, their drug-addicted absent mother and a woman who belonged to them so little Sadie did not miss her. Sadie loved her sister something fierce that if you would swipe her heart searching for fingerprints, you’d find only Mattie’s. She had hung on so long by that single filament of purpose, and the moment she learned of Mattie’s murder, it snapped. Everything and everyone from then on has been lumped with the rest of the world as “<em>not Mattie</em>”, and Sadie’s grief, anger and hatred—as old as herself, and as pure as her love for her sister— lingered and ruled in her stead and prompted her to set out on a dangerous path to find her sister’s murderer…and kill him.<br /><br />Radio personality West McCray, enlisted by Sadie’s surrogate grandmother for help and goaded by his boss, starts a serialized podcast to track Sadie’s journey. McCray leans on the bits and pieces of Sadie’s story that are strewn all around him to learn, messily and gracelessly, the horrifying extent of what happened—truths and secrets that could never be shriven—and his desperation tapers down to a deep pit of need in his gut: <em>find Sadie before it’s too late</em>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“I can’t take another dead girl.”</em>
  <br />
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>Sadie</em> is, to be charitable, an uncomfortable book; but I entirely believe that it's meant to be discomfiting. It is haunting and creepy, a story of loss and lies and betrayal wrapped around a skeleton of heartache and grief. A tale of sisterly devotion that hasn’t tasted any real hope in so long and has been fed and nurtured on darker things—guilt and hurt and so much rage.<br /><br /><strong>We travel the pathways of Sadie’s life and shudder at the horrors there.</strong> Sadie has turned her heart out for the reader to examine the contents. Her voice is visceral, conveying her emotions with startling physicality. It was so deeply heartbreaking to see how much Sadie’s love for her sister inflects her narration, and that sense of marveling at what multitudes could come from one person remained with me throughout the entire book. My desolation deepened at the knowledge that each day, the crank will turn anew, and the gears of the world will lurch into motion but the broken edges of her little sister’s sundered name will not grow smooth with time; Sadie's guilt and grief were corrosive, and she was a husk.<br /><br />Reading this book felt as though I was clinging to the edge of reason by my fingertips, and the spinning world might at any given moment shake me off and hurl me. All I could feel was the approach, the closing-in, and <em>the dread</em>—a clinging, muttering dread, tenacious as cobwebs. My heart was wild with it, and with anguish too, and every new page was scraping a place already raw. I was feeling the story's urgency pull me deeper and deeper inside it and there was only horror as every new truth came clear to me. I genuinely wished that I could somehow form each new revelation into a different picture and disprove my dark suspicions.<br /><br />If you’ve read a Courtney Summers novel, you know that she never pulls her punches, condescends, softens it up or sugarcoats. She knows what teenagers are capable of and what her teenage readers can bear, and she brings both past the very edge of comfort; the result would be either short and abrupt as a firework, or long and spun-out, and you never knew which, the ending might be soft or brutal, and you never knew which.<br /><br /><em>Sadie</em> is a story that confronts you with the gruesome truth that the monsters we conceive in our imagination are not nearly as frightening as the monstrous acts perpetrated by ordinary human beings. That when there isn't even a wisp of humanity to grasp at, let alone a strand to hang on to and follow into the dark, you are only plucking at strings of conscience that will yield no sound.<br /><br /><em>Sadie</em> still keeps replaying itself over and over, relentless, so many questions coiling tightly in my mind, boiling down to one terrible conviction: <strong>I can’t take another dead girl, either</strong>.<br /><br /><strong>TW: </strong>pedophilia, child sexual abuse, parental neglect, mentions and descriptions of substance abuse.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12698826081088288756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1967713085" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1967713085" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1967713085?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1967713085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3715598027502639920"><blockquote>
  <i>And it begins, as so many stories do, with a dead girl.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Holy hell, this book hit me hard.</b><br/><br/>I've been reading Summers' books for seven years now and she is both consistently good and continually getting better. I remember thinking that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a> was one of the most powerful and vicious books I'd ever read back in 2011. Then <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21853636.All_the_Rage' title='All the Rage by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>All the Rage</a> came along and destroyed me some more.<br/><br/>Whether Summers is writing a contemporary high school novel, a mystery, or a zombie apocalypse, she crawls right insid</span>
  <span id="freeText3715598027502639920" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>And it begins, as so many stories do, with a dead girl.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Holy hell, this book hit me hard.</b><br /><br />I've been reading Summers' books for seven years now and she is both consistently good and continually getting better. I remember thinking that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> was one of the most powerful and vicious books I'd ever read back in 2011. Then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21853636.All_the_Rage" title="All the Rage by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Rage</a> came along and destroyed me some more.<br /><br />Whether Summers is writing a contemporary high school novel, a mystery, or a zombie apocalypse, she crawls right inside the deepest, darkest parts of teen girl minds. She explores their grief, their love, their hopes, fears and passions, and she does it in such a way that her characters become unforgettable, feeling at once completely unique AND universal.<br /><br />And this book? <b>This book made me cry</b>. I felt so deeply for Sadie as she goes in search of the man who hurt her sister. Her sister, Mattie, who was her whole world. And yeah, yeah, we've read the "doing it for my sister/brother" a million times in YA but here it's so different. Sadie played the role of mother to Mattie when their own mother disappeared. Their relationship is special; complicated.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“She’s dead,” I whisper and I don’t know why this is the thing I choose to say out loud because it hurts to say it, to feel the truth of those words pass my lips, to have them be real in this world. But She’s dead is the reason I’m still alive.<br />She’s dead is the reason I’m going to kill a man.</i>
</blockquote><br />Sadie goes on a journey from place to place, fighting against her severe stutter along the way, all to find one man. And West McCray’s investigation leads him along the same trail, the before and after racing each other to the end.<br /><br />I think the framing of this story was PERFECT. The author splits the narrative between a radio presenter, West McCray, as he investigates Sadie’s disappearance, and the first person perspective of Sadie herself, as she hunts down her sister’s killer.<br /><br />The juxtaposition of McCray’s detached radio voice with the passion and determination in Sadie’s account works really well. You can just imagine it - Sadie’s story becoming the latest True Crime special - and it honestly hurts to read. You want McCray to just move faster, work harder, <i>care more</i> about this poor girl from a disadvantaged background. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Please save her</b>
</i> was running through my mind the whole time. I felt a little panicked while reading, especially as Sadie becomes ever more reckless. It’s heartbreaking to see this girl who believes she has lost everything important in her world.<br /><br />It could be likened to any book with a badass female character on a mission, from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25812109.The_Female_of_the_Species" title="The Female of the Species by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Female of the Species</a> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/257845.True_Grit" title="True Grit by Charles Portis" rel="nofollow noopener">True Grit</a>, but really, it stands on its own. In the end, it feels like a book about all the ways Sadie is let down by the people who should have helped and protected her; all the ways poor young girls are let down by the people who should have helped and protected them. <br /><br />And still, despite it all, this is a Courtney Summers book, so even at her lowest, weakest moments, Sadie still has claws. The sad thing is that she ever had to use them.<br /><br />TW: Pedophilia; sexual abuse; drug abuse.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3715598027502639920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2524568030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2524568030" />
    <a title="Zoë" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9303625-zo"><img alt="Zoë" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580008879p2/9303625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2524568030?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoë" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoë" href="/user/show/9303625-zo">Zoë</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2524568030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer291658331639917916">CW: Pedophilia, sexual abuse, drug abuse, murder<br/><br/>This was a raw, emotional, and incredibly dark book. There are zero moments of levity and as someone who reads a lot of contemporary romances, it took a lot out of me to get through it. I am grateful that Courtney Summers did not sensationalize any of the abuse that went on before and during the events of this book. Though it's definitely present, it happens off of the page. She focuses on the toll it took on the victims rather than the acts themse</span>
  <span id="freeText291658331639917916" style="display:none">CW: Pedophilia, sexual abuse, drug abuse, murder<br /><br />This was a raw, emotional, and incredibly dark book. There are zero moments of levity and as someone who reads a lot of contemporary romances, it took a lot out of me to get through it. I am grateful that Courtney Summers did not sensationalize any of the abuse that went on before and during the events of this book. Though it's definitely present, it happens off of the page. She focuses on the toll it took on the victims rather than the acts themselves. If you can handle the subject matter (which I wasn't sure I could at first), I'd highly recommend it!<br /><br /><i>Sadie</i> reads like a puzzle, with half of the story being told from Sadie's perspective and half from the perspective of a man doing a podcast on Sadie's disappearance. It's partially up to you to piece together the timeline, which I loved!<br /><br /><u>Make sure you listen to it as an audiobook</u> as it's partially told in the style of a podcast with a large cast of voice actors! They even added ambient noises to set the scenes during interviews. I mean WOW - one of the best audiobook experiences ever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="291658331639917916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2533501534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2533501534" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2533501534?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/40511295-aleksandra">Aleksandra</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2533501534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17607416498792390632"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539371076i/26440689._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I don’t know why this is the thing I choose to say out loud because it hurts to say it, to feel the truth of those words pass my lips, to have them be real in this world. But she’s dead is the reason I’m still alive. She’s dead is the reason I’m going to kill a man.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Sadie</i> is worth all the praise and hype you’ve heard about it. I had a feeling I was going to love this book, but I didn’t know that I would give it a piece of my heart. This is such a bright light in 2018 releases, and e</span>
  <span id="freeText17607416498792390632" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539371076i/26440689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I don’t know why this is the thing I choose to say out loud because it hurts to say it, to feel the truth of those words pass my lips, to have them be real in this world. But she’s dead is the reason I’m still alive. She’s dead is the reason I’m going to kill a man.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Sadie</i> is worth all the praise and hype you’ve heard about it. I had a feeling I was going to love this book, but I didn’t know that I would give it a piece of my heart. This is such a bright light in 2018 releases, and even though it handles some really tough topics, I recommend it with my entire heart and soul. And I will never forget Sadie or her story, and I will never stop listening to, and I will never stop believing, the voices of girls who have their own stories to tell. <br><br>This story is told in alternating chapters between a podcast and Sadie. We follow nineteen-year-old Sadie who is on a mission to murder the person who she believes has murdered her thirteen-year-old sister. The podcast is about five months behind the steps of Sadie, but the two storylines come together so very beautifully. But again, this is a dark book and this review is going to talk about some of those elements, so please use caution. <b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for pedophilia, loss of a loved one, bullying, assault, sexual assault, murder, death, extreme parental abandonment and neglect, talk of suicide, drug use, and underage drinking. <br><br>We get bread crumb after bread crumb from Sadie, while she travels to get revenge for her sister, the only person she has ever loved in this world. And the story really is so expertly crafted with the podcast element. I will say that I did listen to this on audiobook because so many people recommend the story to be experienced that way, but I didn’t love it as much as most people. But then again, I do have a hard time with audiobooks. But I fell so in love with Sadie and her story, that I listened to this in one day and one sitting. <br><br>And I know a lot of people don’t love the ending, but I think it is one of the most powerful endings I’ve probably ever read in my entire life. Plus, I feel like the choice of the cover of <i>Sadie</i> is genius, because Sadie truly is a faceless girl. She is a girl like so many whose stories don’t get to end happily, a girl whose story rarely even gets to be heard, and when it does it isn't believed. <br><br>Something that I think is a really easy concept, but is hard for so many people to understand, is that rapists and pedophiles can be kind, and successful, and funny, and pillars of their community, and it will still never take away from the fact that they are rapists and pedophiles. The other titles and attributes do not lessen the fact that someone is a rapist or a pedophile. And how we teach girls at a very young age that the crimes committed against their bodies, and against their wills, is something to feel shame over. And how we live inside a broken system where rapists can commit the same horrific crime over and over, because no one wants to listen or believe the victims, especially if they are poor and uneducated. And Courtney Summers really illustrates that point so very beautifully throughout <i>Sadie</i>. Because our own world proves every day that people would rather believe powerful men over loud girls. But Sadie takes action into her own hands, and reclaims her power, her body, and her heart, along with getting her vengeance. And it is one of the best journeys I’ve ever experienced. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Sometimes I don’t know what I miss more; everything I’ve lost or everything I never had.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I also want to talk a little bit about the representation in <i>Sadie</i>. First off, Sadie has a very severe stutter. I didn’t know this going in, and as a matter of fact I don’t think I’ve ever read a book where the main character has a stutter before, but it was perfection. Heartbreaking perfection though, because seeing Sadie unable to get the worlds out when she was feeling extreme anger or sadness was so heart wrenching. But Sadie always got the words out, and she always got her hurt across, and it was so beautifully done. Also, I know the scene is brief, but Sadie is so not straight, if anything she sounds rather pan to me. Lastly, Sadie has some of the most realistic poverty rep I’ve ever read, and I still feel like in 2018 that is something that is hard to find. <br><br>And I obviously think <i>Sadie</i> is a masterpiece of a story, and the themes are so important and relevant, but I think the biggest reason I loved this book so much was because I felt so connected to Sadie because of what she felt for Mattie. I will be completely honest with you all, I wouldn’t want to live in a world without my little brother. Me and my brother are a bit closer in age than Mattie and Sadie, and we were never abused or neglected, but the pure unconditional love that Sadie feels for Mattie, and how responsible and protective she felt, it was so pure and so realistic and just completely ripped out my heart and left me feeling so raw and vulnerable. I would do anything in the universe to protect my little brother, and I feel like I fell in love with this book just because Sadie’s love for her sister resonated so strongly in my very soul. There is a line in this book about Sadie feeling alive when her sister comes home from the hospital, and how she laid a hand on her baby sister’s chest and felt her breathing, and I was uncontrollably weeping while reading it. I don’t think I’ve ever seen the love I have for my brother depicted so closely than to that passage, and I know I will carry that inside my heart forever. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I stood over her crib and listened to her breathing, watching the rise and fall of her tiny chest. I pressed my palm against it and felt myself through her. She was breathing, alive. And I was too.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, this book just really meant a lot to me. And even though this book is heartbreaking, it has some of the most beautiful quotes I’ve read all year. I read it with tears in my eyes for at least half, but I wouldn’t trade this reading experience for anything. And I am now going to read every single thing Courtney Summers has created. I truly loved this one, and I recommend it with my entire heart and soul, especially if you have a close sibling relationship, if you enjoy murder mystery podcasts, and if you also want to change the world so that more victims’ voices not only get heard but get believed. <br><br>Lastly, I want anyone who needs to hear it to know two things: First, if you need to talk to someone, <a href="https://www.rainn.org/" rel="nofollow noopener">RAINN</a> is always there. They are completely confidential, and available 24/7. You can also call 800.656.HOPE at any time, too. Secondly, I believe you and your voice deserves to be heard and believed. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/77187817-ashwini-abhyankar" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashwini</a> at <a href="https://bookwormmuse.wordpress.com/2018/11/21/favourite-books-tag/" rel="nofollow noopener">bookwormmuse</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="17607416498792390632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2306284617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2306284617" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2306284617?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-arcs">x-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2018">y-out2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2018">z-faves2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=she-did-that">she-did-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=catharsis-dot-mp3">catharsis-dot-mp3</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2306284617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4871181111855170089"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I didn't know what to tell her. That I tried not to think about that kind of stuff, because it was painful, because I thought I could ever have it, but when I did end up liking someone, it always made me ache right down to my core. I realized pretty early on that the who didn't really matter so much. That anybody who listens to me, I end up loving them just a little.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><u>
  <b>Heartbreaking, hopeful, and impossible to look away from.</b>
</u> <br/><br/>I am really loving this recent trend in YA thrillers of k</span>
  <span id="freeText4871181111855170089" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I didn't know what to tell her. That I tried not to think about that kind of stuff, because it was painful, because I thought I could ever have it, but when I did end up liking someone, it always made me ache right down to my core. I realized pretty early on that the who didn't really matter so much. That anybody who listens to me, I end up loving them just a little.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><u>
  <b>Heartbreaking, hopeful, and impossible to look away from.</b>
</u> <br /><br />I am really loving this recent trend in YA thrillers of killer women. Books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1854035694" rel="nofollow noopener">The Female of the Species</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1549229445" rel="nofollow noopener">Far From You</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2098209026" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Little Lies</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1963538037" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Iris</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1863248823" rel="nofollow noopener">Dangerous Boys</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1817178888" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl from the Well</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1549222094" rel="nofollow noopener">Dare Me</a>. What do all of these have in common? <b>They are about women taking back power from men who hurt women.</b><br /><br />I think the narratives we are used to give men the agency, and it is so interesting to see the trend of women fighting back. <br /><br />So what is this book? <i>Sadie</i> follows podcaster West McCray, a mid20s man investigating a two-sister disappearance for posterity. And in scenes throughout, we see Sadie herself, off to kill her sister’s murderer. <br /><br />There’s not exactly a wide cast of characters for a novel, but Sadie makes up for it. Sadie is such a fantastic lead character; she’s out for a revenge, bitter and angry, a sexual assault victim, pansexual, grew up poor, and has a major stutter. I absolutely adored her, and watching her go further down this awful track was so horrifying. <br /><br />There’s a really interesting element of this book where, at least in the arc copy, no one in the book really does anything beyond imply pedophilia until around 60% of the way through the book, when Sadie asks a man point-blank whether he's a pedophile. It’s a horrifying reality for Sadie; it’s a simple accepted fact of her life. And she attempts to push it down, but when the sentence is finally said, when Sadie finally calls it out, I winced so strongly. That element is just one facet of the horror of this book - that Sadie knows it's wrong, and yet she refuses to say it. <br /><br />Courtney Summers does not shy away from the harsh realities of this world - the contrast between poverty and wealth, the idea that privileged people often get away with horrifying deeds, the lack of agency given to girls in our society. I really think the most accurate description of this is <b>
  <u>stark</u>
</b>. I could not look away, but I think it was worth it. This will haunt me for a very long time. <br /><br />TW: sexual abuse, child abuse, addiction.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4871181111855170089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2514128312" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2514128312" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2514128312?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=dark-and-twisted">dark-and-twisted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=suspense-mystery-thriller">suspense-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2514128312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16461736462118143143">To say I’m not much of a YA reader is underplaying reality a bit. To say that I’m extremely choosy, ready to renege at the first sign of any juvenile antics and pretty much dragging my feet through the first few chapters, when I do finally cave, is all too accurate. My point being, if you’ve hesitated to pick up <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34810320.Sadie' title='Sadie by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sadie</a> because you don’t frequent YA reads, let those preconceived notions go and take a chance. Live life through Sadie’s eyes—I'm betting you <u>won’t</u> regret it. Hers is a bleak and tormen</span>
  <span id="freeText16461736462118143143" style="display:none">To say I’m not much of a YA reader is underplaying reality a bit. To say that I’m extremely choosy, ready to renege at the first sign of any juvenile antics and pretty much dragging my feet through the first few chapters, when I do finally cave, is all too accurate. My point being, if you’ve hesitated to pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34810320.Sadie" title="Sadie by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Sadie</a> because you don’t frequent YA reads, let those preconceived notions go and take a chance. Live life through Sadie’s eyes—I'm betting you <u>won’t</u> regret it. Hers is a bleak and tormenting reality at times, but one worth acknowledging.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"And it begins, as so many stories do, with a dead girl."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Sometimes the story isn’t about the dead 13-year-old girl, left in a field behind a burned out schoolhouse, but rather the disappearance of her nineteen-year-old sister. A girl that took on the mothering role when her own drunk and drugged out mother didn’t care enough to bother. An older sister that did <i>everything</i> in her power to keep her little sister safe . . . until that one moment she took a beat for herself and wasn’t there. One single night—a time out of sorts—that spelled goodbye.<br /><br />Armed with a switchblade to do the dirty work and driven by a thirst for revenge, Sadie sets out to find the monster responsible for killing her sister. She’s gutsy and reckless, but raw and so darn young. Left with a gaping hole her sister once occupied, will happiness ever be an option or is Sadie’s final act imminent? <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I’m going to carve my name into his soul."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />It’s a podcaster that finds himself playing detective, piecing together Sadie’s disappearance for her pseudo-grandmother and his listeners—dueling Sadie’s timeline along the way. Initially denying there was even a story to tell—<i>“Girls go missing all the time.”</i>—until the evidence left him no choice but to succumb to the hunt. <br /><br />The truth is harsh, soul-crushing and just downright awful. I think we can all agree, there’s nothing worse than innocent children being hurt at the hands of a demon and even more so when their parents don’t care enough to pay attention. Knowing there are kids out there living this life right now, makes this story that much harder to stomach.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> gives just enough of the story to make assumptions about the finale—all of the pieces are there, waiting to be assembled as the reader sees fit. My optimistic side liked that she left the door slightly cracked for the teeniest tiniest bit of hope to slip through—although probably <i>extremely</i> unlikely given the evidence—with the only other option being one no one wants to consider. <br /><br />I have to admit, there’s something truly engaging about the author’s style. There’s almost a quiet beauty to the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> strings thoughts together, while simultaneously working to keep the reader in the dark. A few times her words made me pause, reread and reflect—making it easy to see what all the fuss has been about. Like this lovely passage:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I wish this was a love story. A love story about lovers whose mouths meet like two puzzle pieces fitting perfectly into place, about the electric feeling of one person’s name on the other’s tongue because no one has ever spoken them out loud like that before. About people who spend the night together looking at the stars until entire constellations exist within them. Everyone is perfect in that indistinct way most characters are and every perfectly constructed scene in their fictional lives is somehow more real than anything you’ve known or lived."<i></i></i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Regardless of the genre label, Sadie left a mark on my heart. To say that I’m a YA convert—<i>not quite</i>. A new <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> fan—<i>yes!</i><br /><br /><i>**Thank you to St. Martin’s Press &amp; Wednesday Books for a review copy.**</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16461736462118143143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2550735686" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2550735686" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2550735686?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2550735686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16936763969684972652">4.5 stars! I picked this book up on a whim and I GREATLY enjoyed it. This is a must-read for my fans of crime fiction.<br/><br/>CW: sexual abuse, pedophilia, violence, drug abuse, death/murder<br/><br/>I really did not know what to expect from this novel going in. All I knew was that it was half-podcast, half-novel which tells the story of a girl searching for her sister’s killer. I was totally unprepared for the true darkness of this book, which was a (weirdly) wonderful surprise. This is my first read from Courtn</span>
  <span id="freeText16936763969684972652" style="display:none">4.5 stars! I picked this book up on a whim and I GREATLY enjoyed it. This is a must-read for my fans of crime fiction.<br /><br />CW: sexual abuse, pedophilia, violence, drug abuse, death/murder<br /><br />I really did not know what to expect from this novel going in. All I knew was that it was half-podcast, half-novel which tells the story of a girl searching for her sister’s killer. I was totally unprepared for the true darkness of this book, which was a (weirdly) wonderful surprise. This is my first read from Courtney Summers, though I’m aware she does not shy away from tough topics in her books, and the same can be said for <i>Sadie</i>. This is an extremely heavy book that uncovers the evilier side of our society, but it is expressed in a way that is raw, authentic, and not at all sensationalized.<br /><br />I feel the framing of the story is one of it’s shining points. The combination of Sadie’s first-person perspective with the podcast featuring interviews of those she encountered on her journey was truly mesmerizing. If you can, I’d <b>highly</b> recommend the audio version. Full casts are always enjoyable in my opinion, but the production value of this story is off the charts. From added tape-recording sounds to birds chirping in the background, it truly is a full-sensory experience that is far beyond what I typically get out of audiobooks. Piecing the story together through Sadie’s search and Wes’ investigation made for a unique and compelling reading experience. I can say with sincerity, I’ve never read anything like it.<br /><br />The only thing I really struggled with in this novel is that it felt slow at some points. There are some high intensity moments that are true page-turners, but other moments were a little stagnant for me.<br /><br />Overall, <i>Sadie</i> is truly a one-of-a-kind story. I can’t wait to read more from Courtney Summers after such a pleasant time reading my first work of hers.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16936763969684972652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2431079553" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2431079553?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2431079553" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17607653317697138147"><i>((me: disillusionment with the world intensifies))</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550758678ra/27097142.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Alternating between a <i>Serial</i>-type podcast, narrated by a man named West McCray, and Sadie, a teen girl with a need for revenge, this hard-hitting YA Contemporary novel is a <b>gut-punching tour de force of modern-American noir</b>. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456182800ra/18200863.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>By the time she has reached her mid-teens, Sadie has accepted the fact that she is the main caregiver for her little sister, Mattie. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551277472ra/27125565.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Although dealing with Mattie can be infuriating at times, Sadie loves her with her whole hea</span>
  <span id="freeText17607653317697138147" style="display:none"><i>((me: disillusionment with the world intensifies))</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550758678ra/27097142.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alternating between a <i>Serial</i>-type podcast, narrated by a man named West McCray, and Sadie, a teen girl with a need for revenge, this hard-hitting YA Contemporary novel is a <b>gut-punching tour de force of modern-American noir</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456182800ra/18200863.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>By the time she has reached her mid-teens, Sadie has accepted the fact that she is the main caregiver for her little sister, Mattie. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551277472ra/27125565.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Although dealing with Mattie can be infuriating at times, Sadie loves her with her whole heart and has done her best to provide a safe environment for them both. <br><br>Their mother, a junkie, whose biggest concern is what man she'll be hooking up with next, has failed to provide the girls with a stable home. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551277472ra/27125566.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sadie has never felt loved by her mother and this lack of connection displays itself through her outlook on the world. <br><br>Jaded and cynical, Sadie has good reason to be, her situation only made more difficult by the severe stutter that has plagued her since early childhood. Her stutter makes it challenging for her to express herself, and because of this, she feels judged and underestimated by many people.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551277472ra/27125567.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When her mother runs off again, seemingly for good this time, Sadie's fate is sealed. She is left to provide for Mattie around the clock. <br><br>After a fight regarding their mother's whereabouts, Mattie flees their home, only to be discovered later, murdered. <br><br>Sadie, overcome with anger and despair, is determined to track down Mattie's killer and bring him to justice. In fact, she knows who killed her and won't rest until he pays.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551277472ra/27125568.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As sad as this story is, it is boldly realistic and I respect the fact that Summers never shied away from tough, taboo topics. <br><br>I would recommend if you are a sensitive reader, you check other reviews for trigger warnings.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551277472ra/27125569.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I listened to the audiobook for this, while also reading the hardcover version. The audiobook is definitely worth listening to. <br><br>The podcast sections were particularly well done and I do believe listening to it enhanced my overall reading experience.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534729102ra/26159449.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While I did enjoy this a lot, I wasn't as blown away by it as others seemed to be. It was really well told and the topics were well handled.<br><br>I just think the hype made me expect a little more. I read a lot of gritty, dark stories, so nothing about this surprised me or felt particularly groundbreaking besides the format.<br><br>Overall, the story is depressing, but important. I would recommend it to anyone, particularly the audiobook.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17607653317697138147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2289418519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2289418519" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2289418519?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=feminist-as-fuck">feminist-as-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=important">important</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2289418519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer382900116954574042"><i>"Imagine having to live every day knowing the person who killed your sister is breathing the air she can't, filling his lungs with it, tasting its sweetness. Imagine him knowing the steady weight of the earth under his feet while her body is buried six feet below it."</i><br/><br/><i>Sadie</i> was everything I wished and more than I could have fathomed.<br/>I always try to keep my expectations low, especially if it’s a debut author, an overhyped book or a book by an author that I’ve never read before. If I do not keep my</span>
  <span id="freeText382900116954574042" style="display:none"><i>"Imagine having to live every day knowing the person who killed your sister is breathing the air she can't, filling his lungs with it, tasting its sweetness. Imagine him knowing the steady weight of the earth under his feet while her body is buried six feet below it."</i><br /><br /><i>Sadie</i> was everything I wished and more than I could have fathomed.<br />I always try to keep my expectations low, especially if it’s a debut author, an overhyped book or a book by an author that I’ve never read before. If I do not keep my expectations in check, they will get out of control, like children running towards a playground, screaming from excitement. And then they realise the swings and everything else has been burned down. Yeah. I don’t want my expectations burned to the ground. I don’t want any crying children. <br /><i>Sadie</i>, however, added a swimming pool, a bouncy castle and a super cool cave to the playground. But don’t kid yourself, this book is so not funny. I actually want to join the crying children, that’s how depressing it was. Aaand this metaphor officially got out of hands. What I'm trying to say is, if you're ever in the mood for a gut punch, this is your book. It hurts so much because it's real. It's a vicious story, but it's not a fantasy book, it's not a fairytale set in a faraway land. And Sadie is so vulnerable and lonely. She doesn't deserve any of the things that have happened to her because nobody deserves anything like this. But you cannot help her, you cannot take away her loneliness and misery and that realisation will crush you.<br /><br />I honestly cannot find anything to criticise. And I’m nitpicky, believe me. So if you want my word for it, just go and read the book now or pick up the fantastic audiobook. Because from here on this review will stop being spoiler-free.<br />The characters are fantastic. Sadie is absolutely relatable. She is a caring, protective woman who will fight with everything she’s got for the people she loves. Her life is far from easy; many would go so far and say that it sucks big time. But she has her sister, Mattie, and that’s a life worth living.<br />When Mattie is found dead, Sadie’s world shatters to pieces. But she knows who killed her and she will find a way to take revenge for every injustice that has been done to her sister – and to herself. Sadie disappears. And here, Wes McCray joins the game.<br /><br />West McCray is a journalist who stumbles upon the story of a girl found dead and a second girl reported missing. His side of the story is told in the form of a podcast titled The Girls. On his journey to find Sadie he interviews a great number of people and reports all his findings to his listeners. The combination of these two narratives – Sadie’s point of view and Wes’ podcast – was so intriguing that I could not close the book. That and the excruciating cliffhangers at the end of every chapter nearly killed me. And killed one or the other fictional character in the process.<br /><br />I will shove this book under every person’s nose who will tell me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114135.All_the_Ugly_and_Wonderful_Things" title="All the Ugly and Wonderful Things by Bryn Greenwood" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Ugly and Wonderful Things</a> is suuuuch a good book. Sadie is the anti-christ to<i>All the Ugly and Wonderful Things</i>. Or rather, the Harry to his Voldemort.<br />If you have not already realised it yourself, adult men who have sex with children and teenagers are scum. And Sadie has come to end them. This book is basically YA Kill Bill.<br /><br />I appreciated that the author managed to not shy away from the grim reality of sexual abuse while staying away from painting a too vivid and explicit picture of the horrible crimes at the same time. It left enough room for your imagination to fill the gaps and protected the reader – especially younger ones – from possible nightmares.<br /><br />Also, let’s talk about sexuality. We’re finally at this stage (at least in YA literature) where a character’s sexuality doesn’t define their plot. It’s a part of them that is no longer discussed, like the fact that someone’s favourite colour is blue. I know it sounds stupid to point this out, but it made me so happy. Every time in this novel when a character’s sexuality was brought up, it lacked a positive/negative/surprised reaction because PEOPLE ARE GAY KAREN GET OVER IT.<br /><br />Sadie was one of my favourite reads of 2018 and I hope it will get super famous so that I can talk to people about it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="382900116954574042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2387159324" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2387159324" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2387159324?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=powerful">powerful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387159324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15785232066158559685"><b>*5 solid stars!*<br/><br/><i>"I’m dangerous. You shouldn't underestimate people, I want to call out. I have a knife."</i></b><br/><br/><b>SADIE</b> has lost herself and she doesn't want to be found. Not by the few remaining people in her life, not even by life itself. She lets the reader know right away that she is being fueled only by revenge, and there is no question that Sadie is surviving for the sole purpose of killing the man she believes murdered her little sister. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>"I’m going to kill a man. I’m going to steal the light fro</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText15785232066158559685" style="display:none"><b>*5 solid stars!*<br><br><i>"I’m dangerous. You shouldn't underestimate people, I want to call out. I have a knife."</i></b><br><br><b>SADIE</b> has lost herself and she doesn't want to be found. Not by the few remaining people in her life, not even by life itself. She lets the reader know right away that she is being fueled only by revenge, and there is no question that Sadie is surviving for the sole purpose of killing the man she believes murdered her little sister. <br><br><i>
  <b>"I’m going to kill a man. I’m going to steal the light from his eyes. I want to watch it go out."</b>
</i><br><br>This was a heinous crime whose victim has obtained no justice; a case gone cold, until Sadie herself goes missing and the host of a serialized podcast is persuaded to revive it. <br><br>The podcast portions are handled extremely well and are delivered in chapters that alternate with the saturated darkness of Sadie’s first-person narrative. We get right in her head, and it is wholly intense at the very least. <br><br>I would say that Sadie’s falling apart, but that would imply she’d once had it all together, and she has <i>never</i>. Not with an absentee father, and an addict of a mother. Not when she’d been forced to raise her younger sister as though she wasn't also just a child herself. <br><br>Sadie has stripped away the outer layers of herself until all that remains is this primal, animalistic being whose desire to kill this man has become the only thing in life that matters. I could sense her wasting away, eating only because she has to and because not eating would steal the strength she needs to carry out her plan. <br><br>You will feel Sadie’s desperation as it all but suffocates her. You will witness her becoming a machine—one who feels only pain, if she feels anything at all. Her eyes are focused, and she’s seeing red as she paves her own way through the road splayed out in front of her—god help anyone who tries to stand in her way. <br><br><b>Courtney Summer’s</b> writing continually impresses me, and frankly just keeps getting better. I’ve come to love the sharpened edges of her young adult stories, but this one in particular seems to break through the confines of YA altogether, targeting a much wider audience than teens. <br><br>This plot is driven; a reckless drive, and it’s Sadie behind the wheel, the reader sitting shotgun alongside her. It’s brave and it’s raw and it feels so close to <u>real</u> that you may just have to remind yourself to come up for air at times. <br><br>Sadie’s character, with all of her pain, is sharp and witty, and even funny at times. She speaks with a stutter, which only endeared me to her even more, and she’s easy to love even though she’s not intentionally casting out lovable vibes. <br><br>Every element in the story came to life—all of it—and it wasn't pretty to look at, but it was powerful and it was important. A mother’s addiction. A sister’s reliance. A child abused. A daughter, so in need of her mother’s love that the lack of it has hollowed out her insides, leaving a hole that can only be filled with pain and uncertainty. <br><br><b>
  <i>"Sometimes I don’t know what I miss more; everything I’ve lost or everything I never had."</i>
</b><br><br>This book is more than a story—it is a voice, and it begs to be heard. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪  Genre/Category:</b> Contemporary/Young Adult/Mystery<br><b>▪  Characters:</b> Sadie's character is sole focus of story. She's painfully broken and highly driven in her pursuit. <br><b>▪  Plot:</b> Sadie sets out to kill the man she believes murdered her sister. <br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Edgy, witty, brilliant! This author is a favorite of mine!<br><b>▪ POV:</b> 1st Person Perspective: Alternates between Sadie's POV and Podcast transcripts <br><b>▪  Cliffhanger:</b> None. Standalone<br><br><i>*Thanks to St. Martin’s Press for providing an advanced digital copy via Netgalley!*</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15785232066158559685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2291406806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2291406806" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2291406806?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=girls-gone-wild">girls-gone-wild</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=grgiveaways">grgiveaways</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291406806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer201915087884567845"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best YA 2018! what will happen?</b><br/><br/><i>In our last episode, I introduced you to the two girls at the center of this podcast, Mattie Southern and Sadie Hunter. Mattie was murdered, her body left just outside her hometown of Cold Creek, Colorado. Sadie is missing, her car found, abandoned, thousands of miles away, with all her personal belongings still inside it. The girls’ surrogate grandmother, May Beth Foster, has enlisted my help in finding Sadie and brin</i></span>
  <span id="freeText201915087884567845" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best YA 2018! what will happen?</b><br><br><i>In our last episode, I introduced you to the two girls at the center of this podcast, Mattie Southern and Sadie Hunter. Mattie was murdered, her body left just outside her hometown of Cold Creek, Colorado. Sadie is missing, her car found, abandoned, thousands of miles away, with all her personal belongings still inside it. The girls’ surrogate grandmother, May Beth Foster, has enlisted my help in finding Sadie and bringing her home.<br><br>For those of you just tuning in, this is a serialized podcast, so if you haven’t listened to our first episode, you should do that now. We have more story than time to tell it - but I suppose that’s true for all of us.</i><br><br>this book is such a ballpunch. <br><br>i don’t even <i>have</i> balls, but i felt it - the sharp whitehot flashes of sudden impact; boof, boof, boof, followed by a deep nausea.<br><br>courtney summers is gonna ballpunch all of you. <br><br>this book’s got some things in common with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25812109.The_Female_of_the_Species" title="The Female of the Species by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Female of the Species</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30753570.Are_You_Sleeping" title="Are You Sleeping by Kathleen Barber" rel="nofollow noopener">Are You Sleeping</a>, but it has a ferocity all its own, and as much as i loved the fierce energy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25812109.The_Female_of_the_Species" title="The Female of the Species by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Female of the Species</a>, with its teengirl vigilantism and <i>Hard Candy</i> revenge-killings, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34810320.Sadie" title="Sadie by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Sadie</a> is much darker and more realistic, which makes it much, much scarier. and if there are still any adults out there who think they are 'too grown' for YA books, think again, because although this is targeted at a teen audience, the quality of summers’ writing is better than many adult-market books i’ve read, and she doesn’t pull any of those punches - they hit and hit hard. <br><br>there are two narrative voices: the rawnerve howl of nineteen-year-old sadie, on the trail of the man she believes killed her thirteen-year-old sister mattie, and west mccray - the creator of the podcast <i>The Girls</i>, whose contributions are mostly in the form of transcripts from that podcast, with all the rounded-edged detached professional compassion of an NPR host. <br><br>sadie has zero rounded edges left. all she has is a car, a backpack, some cash, and a plan:<br><br><blockquote>”She’s dead,” I whisper and I don’t know why this is the thing I choose to say out loud because it hurts to say it, to feel the truth of those words pass my lips, to have them be real in this world. But <i>She’s dead</i> is the reason I’m still alive.<br><br><i>She’s dead</i> is the reason I’m going to kill a man.</blockquote><br><br>sadie dropped out of school at sixteen to raise her sister after their addict-mother left, both of their fathers long out of the picture, and she struggled for years to make ends meet with her truncated education and severe stutter in a small-town trailer park full of bad memories and no prospects for the future.<br><br><i>For some people, the future ahead is opportunity. For others, it’s only time you haven’t met and where I lived, it was only time. You don’t waste your breath trying to protect it. You just try to survive it until one day, you don’t.</i><br><br>what she did have was her devotion to mattie, and with mattie gone, she’s got nothing left to lose and she’s a mama-bear incandescent with vengeance. <br><br>i'll say no more, but oh, man, this is a powerhouse of a book. it'll getcha.<br><br>***************************************<br><br>might bump this up to five stars - gotta let it all settle. <br>review to come, but in short: magnificent.<br><br>***************************************<br><br>it's here!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522590289i/25306590._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>***************************************<br><br><i>Congratulations karen!<br><br>You are one of our Giveaways lucky winners! </i><br><br>YYYEEEAAAAHHHHH!! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521906007ra/25268149.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="201915087884567845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
