<div id="review_2535036677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2535036677" />
    <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks"><img alt="BernLuvsBooks " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585010050p2/3087404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2535036677?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=fave-reads">fave-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2535036677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6057338278366359909"><b>
  <i>"When Sadie lost Mattie, it drove her to leave her home in Cold Creek, to take on the loneliness and pain of all those miles, just to find her little sister's murderer and make the world right again, even, possibly, at the expense of herself."</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Sadie was everything I hoped she would be and more!</b> She is the kind of character that tays with you long after you have finished reading the book.<br/><br/>Sadie has had a hard life but nothing affects her more deeply than the murder of her sister. It was a horri</span>
  <span id="freeText6057338278366359909" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"When Sadie lost Mattie, it drove her to leave her home in Cold Creek, to take on the loneliness and pain of all those miles, just to find her little sister's murderer and make the world right again, even, possibly, at the expense of herself."</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Sadie was everything I hoped she would be and more!</b> She is the kind of character that tays with you long after you have finished reading the book.<br /><br />Sadie has had a hard life but nothing affects her more deeply than the murder of her sister. It was a horrific crime and it seems no one will answer for it. Sadie simply cannot accept that. She has nothing left to live for - except seeking her own brand of justice for her sister. <br /><br />Sadie ultimately ghosts. She walks away from the life she knows, seeking revenge, armed with a switchblade and fueled by sheer determination. Sadie's story is harsh and simply heart crushing. She is the kind of character that you wish you could reach inside of the book and save. Except Sadie didn't want saving. She was beyond that. <br /><br />The story is told from alternating viewpoints - that of Sadie and radio personality, West McCray. West McCray is called in to help find Sadie by her neighbor, who was essentially looking out for her and Mattie. He decides to follow the clues as part of his podcast in the hopes that the trail of crumbs will lead him to Sadie. <br /><br />This book was so well crafted. Summers does an amazing job of pulling the reader into Sadie's world. We feel her grief and her anger. We see the effects of her pain. We can't help but love her for it because we know Sadie needs and deserves our love. The love she never felt from her mother. The love she has craved all her life and had freely given to her sister. <br /><br />This is not a happy story. It speaks of child abuse, murder, substance abuse, parental neglect and more. This story broke me and yet I feel better for having read it. <b>Sadie is one of those rare characters that will live on in my heart.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6057338278366359909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2429395356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2429395356" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2429395356?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=disability-and-mi">disability-and-mi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2429395356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4321374372474113552">At the time I’m writing this review, it’s been a couple of days since I finished <i>Sadie</i>, and I still haven’t fully processed it. This is one of those stories that seeps into your bones somewhere along the way, and it changes the way you look at the world a little. It is the best mystery—and one of the best books, period—that I have ever read, and it is also one of the bleakest, most devastating reading experiences of my life. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>And it begins, as so many stories do, with a dead girl.</b>
</blockquote><br/>You know, go</span>
  <span id="freeText4321374372474113552" style="display:none">At the time I’m writing this review, it’s been a couple of days since I finished <i>Sadie</i>, and I still haven’t fully processed it. This is one of those stories that seeps into your bones somewhere along the way, and it changes the way you look at the world a little. It is the best mystery—and one of the best books, period—that I have ever read, and it is also one of the bleakest, most devastating reading experiences of my life. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>And it begins, as so many stories do, with a dead girl.</b>
</blockquote><br />You know, going into this story, that Sadie’s little sister’s body has just been found, and Sadie is on a mission to track down the man she believes is responsible. Besides the fact that it’s a story partially told through <b>podcast episodes</b> (which is such an incredible touch), that’s all you really <i>need</i> to know. This isn’t about what happens so much as it is about coming to know and love Sadie—and to know and love Mattie, too, through her memories. It’s about recognizing that the society we live in has this terrifying, grimy layer that nobody wants to talk about, where little girls are never <i>really</i> safe, and children are forced to grow up way too fast, to become adults in replacement of the parents they didn’t ask for.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>Imagine having to live every day knowing the person who killed your sister is breathing the air she can’t, filling his lungs with it, tasting its sweetness. Imagine him knowing the steady weight of the earth under his feet while her body is buried six feet below it.</b>
</blockquote><br />With a mother suffering from addiction, a community that looked the other way far too many times, and a life of barely keeping food on the table, much less having any real opportunities to succeed, Sadie feels like such an old soul. I don’t know how many readers will struggle to relate to the <i>age</i> of her inner monologue, but from another woman whose circumstances never quite allowed me to feel like a child, I saw so much of myself in the cynical, pragmatic way Sadie views the world around her.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>I realized pretty early on that the who didn’t really matter so much. That anybody who listens to me, I end up loving them just a little.</b>
</blockquote><br />It’s hard enough to grow up poor and in a broken family, but Sadie’s also queer—she doesn’t label herself, but explains her sexuality in ways that heavily point to pansexuality—and she stutters, which forms a barricade between her and the rest of the world. Her representation feels so valid and genuine, and it broke my heart every time she mused about how imprisoned she felt by her struggles with speech.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>I’d do it all again and again for eternity if I had to. I don’t know why that’s not enough to bring her back.</b>
</blockquote><br />More than anything else about Sadie’s character, though, I loved the fierce, maternal determination she has for taking care of Mattie—and, once Mattie is gone, for finding her killer and dishing out justice. Every memory of Mattie, whether told through her view of their adopted grandmother May Beth’s, is beautiful and haunting. The tremendous amount of guilt that Sadie carries as she blames herself for what went wrong had me completely breaking down in passages, and I’ll admit without shame that I read the last several chapters through tears. The most brutal part of it all is that, somehow, it feels like Sadie’s story could be based on a real girl—no, on countless real girls, all over the world.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>I have never been kissed the way I want to be kissed and I have never been touched the way I want to be touched.</b>
</blockquote><br />Without spoiling the plot, I want to warn you that <b>this book focuses heavily on child abuse and sexual assault,</b> and it is broken down in the most honest, agonizing ways. There’s also a solid portrayal of how deceptive abusers can be, as the abusers in question are shown to have fooled so many people. But there’s also another side to the representation here, as we see Sadie’s intense solidarity with other abused girls, and her desperate need to protect and defend them, even though (perhaps <i>especially</i> though) she feels that she failed to protect and defend her sister.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>It’s about the lengths we go to protect the ones we love… and the high price we pay when we can’t.</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />There’s not much else I can tell you now, because I think it’s the kind of story that you should go into without too many expectations. Just climb in, let <i>Sadie</i> take you for a ride and tell you her story, and try not to let your heart get <i>too</i> broken in the process. This is a phenomenal story, and I know that I will be thinking about it for a long, long time to come.<br /><br /><b>Content warnings</b> for child abuse, sexual assault, drug addiction, addiction-shaming, PTSD, violence, child abduction, child death<br /><br /><i>All quotes come from an advance copy and may not match the final release. Thank you so much to Wednesday Books for providing me with this ARC in exchange for an honest review!</i><br /><br />You can find this review and more on my <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2018/08/15/sadie/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>, or you can follow me on <a href="https://twitter.com/howlinglibrary" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>, <a href="https://instagram.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">bookstagram</a>, or <a href="https://facebook.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4321374372474113552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2376148110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376148110" />
    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2376148110?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376148110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4050549359351068567">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/'>https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>19 year old, Sadie and her younger sister, Mattie struggled to get by. Cold Creek is a small town with very few opportunities for employment. Many have to go to a neighboring town for work and school.<br/><br/>Mary Beth Foster was Mattie and Sadie's neighbor and the manager of the trailer park where they lived. Mary Beth tried to look out for the sisters but basically, it was just the two of them. Their mother, Claire had been out of </span>
  <span id="freeText4050549359351068567" style="display:none">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br />19 year old, Sadie and her younger sister, Mattie struggled to get by. Cold Creek is a small town with very few opportunities for employment. Many have to go to a neighboring town for work and school.<br /><br />Mary Beth Foster was Mattie and Sadie's neighbor and the manager of the trailer park where they lived. Mary Beth tried to look out for the sisters but basically, it was just the two of them. Their mother, Claire had been out of the picture for quite a while. <br /><br />The bond between the sisters was very strong, but something horrific happens that severs that bond forever. Now Sadie is missing and Mary Beth Foster just wants to find someone who can help. Someone who will give a damn...<br /><br />West McCray is a radio personality who just happens to overhear a little bit of Sadie and Mattie’s story. At first, he thinks what many others seem to be thinking…<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“Girls run away all the time; girls go missing, there isn’t anything new here.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />West and his producer have been talking about West hosting his own podcast. His producer is the one who suggests he dig a little deeper into Sadie's story. West doesn't really want to do it at first, but finds that he can't stop thinking about their story and ends up creating a serialized podcast called “<strong>The Girls</strong>”<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“when a devastating crime reveals a deeply unsettling mystery.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />After working on the story for awhile, West starts to get nervous. He's scared of what he might find.<br /><br />"<em>
  <strong>If you want the truth, I didn't even want this story. And the more I have it, the less I want it because I don't think it's headed anywhere good. But I'm in this now, so I have to see it through." </strong>
</em><br /><br />So where is Sadie? What or who is she looking for?<br /><br />I thought this was an incredible read. A fantastic and powerfully written story. I was addicted and hated having to put the book down.<br /><br />I thought the layout of the novel was interesting and the characters all very well developed. We get to hear from many people that knew Sadie and Mattie which was a great addition to the story. The story jumps back and forth between Sadie’s journey and “<strong>The Girls</strong>” podcast whose investigation retraces Sadie's steps. The novel deals with some tough subject matter, but I thought the author handled these issues with sensitivity and respect. I was hooked from start to finish.<br /><br />"<strong>Sadie</strong>" is a compelling and riveting story about love, loss, revenge, and the power of a sister's love.<br /><br />I'd like to thank Wednesday Books for giving me the opportunity to read this book in exchange for my honest review.</span>

<div id="review_2335865607" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2335865607" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2335865607?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2550422-st-martin-s-press">St. Martin&#39;s Press</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=giveaways">giveaways</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2335865607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer228946771196570215"><b>Happy Pub Day!!!</b><br/><br/><i>"I'm going to kill a man. I'm going to steal the light from his eyes. I want to watch it go out. You aren't supposed to answer violence with more violence but sometimes I think violence is the only answer."</i><br/><br/>Reading <i>Sadie</i> was the perfect example of why sometimes, the timing of picking up a book can make or break your experience. I tried to pick this one up months ago when I first received it and only made it about 25 pages before I had to place it to the side. I had some heavy stuf</span>
  <span id="freeText228946771196570215" style="display:none"><b>Happy Pub Day!!!</b><br /><br /><i>"I'm going to kill a man. I'm going to steal the light from his eyes. I want to watch it go out. You aren't supposed to answer violence with more violence but sometimes I think violence is the only answer."</i><br /><br />Reading <i>Sadie</i> was the perfect example of why sometimes, the timing of picking up a book can make or break your experience. I tried to pick this one up months ago when I first received it and only made it about 25 pages before I had to place it to the side. I had some heavy stuff going on in my personal life, and I think a book of this calibre wasn't helping me to escape in the form that I needed at the moment. Fast forward to this week and I decided, at the recommendation of many bookstagram friends, to pick this one up again for my readathon. That choice ended up being one of the best decisions I made, as I connected so well to <i>Sadie</i> this go around. All this to say, if you're in a heavy or emotional place in your life right now, you may want to hold off until the opportune moment to pick this one up. <br /><br />If you're looking for a unique novel that is a mature form of YA, this is it. The story is well written, gripping, and emotional, and the podcast format that is becoming so popular amongst authors and readers alike is a slam dunk here. I've heard also that Macmillan is releasing an actual podcast that coincides with the novel every Tuesday/Wednesday ish, and I plan on checking this out in greater detail over the weekend. <i>Sadie</i>, the novel, was an atmospheric read, and its claustrophobic nature had me tugging at the collar of my shirt by the end of the book to try and relieve the pressure that was building from my throat to my stomach. The pacing starts out very slowly, and builds momentum along with the tension that grows as our hearts become chained to Sadie's. <br /><br /><b>It's a tough read guys.</b> I know I've said that about three times now, but I can't stress enough how heavy, yet timely this book is. If you're looking for a happily ever after, a story of redemption, or even just a book that will allow you to sleep again at night once you've finished it, you won't find that here. Without giving away any spoilers, you can expect some questions to be answered, but to be wrestling with the remainder for weeks to come after turning that final page. The alternating between podcast episodes and Sadie's own voice really worked well here, and toward the end there's a switch that just about crippled me once I realized what was being done. While not for the sensitive reader (CW for child abuse, pedophilia, rape, drug and alcohol abuse by minors and adults, graphic violence, etc.), I have to admit that this is a book that many people can learn from, both teens and adults alike. I have a sinking sensation that I'll be grappling with the effects of this book for months to come in my everyday life-when I'm in the shower or driving down the road-and I'll be reminded to hold my daughters a little more closely, because there are so many little girls out there who live a much different life than my babies do, and it's just not fair. <br /><br /><b>Book #1 in my August #25infive readathon.</b><br /><br /><i>Thank you Goodreads Giveaways for my review copy! </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="228946771196570215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3476475615" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3476475615" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3476475615?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3476475615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12514097178414680969"><i>”For some people, the future ahead is opportunity. For others, it’s only time you haven’t met and where I lived, it was only time. You don’t waste your breath trying to protect it. You just try to survive it until one day, you don’t.”</i> <br/><br/>My first reaction when I finished this book was:<br/><b>THIS BOOK WILL HAUNT ME FOR THE REST OF MY LIFE.</b><br/><br/>And I still stand by my initial response. Never in my entire life have I read a book that haunts me as much as <b>“Sadie”</b> does and quite honestly: I hope I’ll never ever re</span>
  <span id="freeText12514097178414680969" style="display:none"><i>”For some people, the future ahead is opportunity. For others, it’s only time you haven’t met and where I lived, it was only time. You don’t waste your breath trying to protect it. You just try to survive it until one day, you don’t.”</i> <br /><br />My first reaction when I finished this book was:<br /><b>THIS BOOK WILL HAUNT ME FOR THE REST OF MY LIFE.</b><br /><br />And I still stand by my initial response. Never in my entire life have I read a book that haunts me as much as <b>“Sadie”</b> does and quite honestly: I hope I’ll never ever read another book like it ever again. &gt;_&lt; This book was so tough to read and whenever I picked it up I found myself taking a deep breath before I could dive back in. I had to prepare for this story because it’s such a heavy one and believe me when I say that I barely made it through the entire book.<br /><br />Not because it wasn’t good, but because it felt like I’d choke on my own feelings whenever I read it. As a loving parent “Sadie” was exceptionally hard to digest and it’s eerie and haunting atmosphere only made it even harder to continue. I’m going to be honest here: I hated almost all of the adults in this book because they <b>JUST DIDN’T CARE!!!</b> Who lets a young 19 year old girl run around in the world without any guidance? So many people crossed Sadie’s path but almost none of them tried to help her and even less tried to convince her to stay, let alone to get some sort of aid. <br /><br /><i>”I can’t undo everything that’s already been done. How do you forgive the people who are supposed to protect you? Sometimes I don’t know what I miss more: everything I ‘ve lost or everything I never had.”</i><br /><br />I for my part can’t forgive the people who were supposed to protect Mattie and Sadie. They all failed and none of them, none of them was there for those two girls when they needed it the most. Yes, May Beth tried and true, West McCray did his best to find Sadie but the rest of them? Caddy, Silas, Marlee, Ellis, Clair Southern (Sadie’s and Mattie’s mother I may add!!) they were all horrible adults and I really hope that karma will bite them in their asses. XD Sure, some of them might have been overtaxed with their own lives and troubles, but they all had a chance to do what’s right and none of them went for it. &gt;_&lt; When given the choice they always chose themselves. <br /><br /><i>”I forget that at times, I was a kid, that I did kid things. That I read about the girls I dreamed of being.”</i><br /><br />And because of actions like that, because of their neglect, Mattie died and Sadie went on a journey to revenge her sister’s murder. She left everything she ever knew behind because she was determined to kill the man who murdered the only person that meant the world to her. Sadie isn’t on a quest, she’s on a mission and it’s to find the bastard who killed her sister and to put him six feet under, no matter the consequences, no matter the cost. It’s a road trip of sorts, and Sadie is driven by anger and revenge. By a sheer insatiable hunger to get rid of the one thing that destroyed her entire world; to stop him from doing the same to others. To end him before he ends anyone else. <br /><br /><i>”In Mattie, Sadie found a sense of purpose, a place to put her love. But love is complicated, it’s messy. It can inspire selflessness, selfishness, our greatest accomplishments and our hardest mistakes. It brings us together and it can just as easily drive us apart.<br /><br />It can drive us.”</i><br /><br />I was with Sadie every step of the way. I suffered with her, I bled with her, I hurt with her, I despaired and cried with her, and I felt her profound and all-consuming grief! I felt what Sadie felt and I admired her resilience. This girl! This girl is one of the bravest I ever read about. The guilt that consumed her, the conviction that she could have done something, anything to save her sister’s life... Gods, at times it was so overwhelming the ink spilled from the pages and punctured my heart. T_T<br /><br /><i>”Thirteen, Mattie.<br />I kept you alive for thirteen years.<br />Waking her up in the morning, making her meals, walking her to the school bus, waiting for her at its stop when the day was over, grinding my bones to dust just to keep us holding on and when I lay it out like that, I don’t know how I did it. I don’t know where, underneath it all, you’d find my body. And I don’t care. I’d do it all again and again for eternity if I had to.<br />I don’t know why that’s not enough to bring her back.”</i><br /><br />Sadie wasn’t just Mattie’s sister, she was her friend, her partner in crime and most of all... she was her mother. The love she felt for her sister, it was the purest thing and it was taken away from her. Violently and brutally. It’s no wonder Sadie harbours vengeful thoughts. Every mile hurt, every second was painful and with every city she leaves the inevitable pinnacle draws closer. And all the time West and May Beth are retracing and following her steps, trying to find a girl that is close to come unglued. At the risk of repeating myself: It’s haunting, it’s eerie, it’s urgent and it’s insistent in its intensity. <br /><br /><i>”I’m going to kill a man.<br />I’m going to steal the light from his eyes. I want to watch it go out. You aren’t supposed to answer violence with more violence but sometimes I think violence is the only answer. It’s no less than he did to Mattie, so it’s no less than he deserves.”</i><br /><br />I’m still not over <b>“Sadie”</b> and I get the feeling I’ll never be. This book was unlike anything I ever read and its vehemence will stick with me for years to come. As will one of the first sentences of this book:<br /><i>”I can’t take another dead girl.”</i><br /><br />Neither can I. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br />trigger warnings: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[murder, paedophilia, sexual abuse, child abuse, violence, addiction &amp; drug abuse, parental negligence, assault <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />________________________________<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THIS BOOK WILL HAUNT ME FOR THE REST OF MY LIFE.</u>
</b><br />I’m... <br />I have no words. I can’t.<br /><br />Just let me digest this for a while...<br /><br />RTC soon! I need to find my voice first.<br />________________________________<br /><br />For a while this book was all over my feed and everybody talked about <b>“Sadie”</b>.<br />The story itself sounds interesting but not like something I’d usually read. Since I’m intent on breaking my reading habits it sounds like the perfect book for me though. <br /><br />So many of my favourite bloggers loved this and I finally want to find out why. <br />It certainly sounds like <b>"Sadie”</b> might have the potential to destroy me and I don’t know if I should look forward to that or be afraid. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br />Either way, let’s find out what happened to Mattie.<br />Something tells me this is going to be a tough read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12514097178414680969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2464039819?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2464039819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17298512807597083976"><b>“I’m going to kill the man who killed my sister.” <br/><br/><i> Sadie is a stunning, heartbreaking read about a girl dead set on murdering the man who killed her little sister. </i></b><br/><br/>19-year-old Sadie only had one thing her life to love, which was her 13-year-old little sister, Mattie. Growing up in a trailer park in Colorado, she had to endure her mother’s drug abuse, neglect, and many boyfriends; some of whom were verbally, physically, and sexually abusive. But Sadie survived in order to protect Mattie. Sadly wh</span>
  <span id="freeText17298512807597083976" style="display:none"><b>“I’m going to kill the man who killed my sister.” <br /><br /><i> Sadie is a stunning, heartbreaking read about a girl dead set on murdering the man who killed her little sister. </i></b><br /><br />19-year-old Sadie only had one thing her life to love, which was her 13-year-old little sister, Mattie. Growing up in a trailer park in Colorado, she had to endure her mother’s drug abuse, neglect, and many boyfriends; some of whom were verbally, physically, and sexually abusive. But Sadie survived in order to protect Mattie. Sadly when Mattie is murdered, Sadie is intent on seeking revenge on the man who killed Mattie.<br /><br />Sadie is a sharp, intelligent, edgy character. There’s nothing smooth about her and wherever she goes, she leaves a mark. That’s why when an investigation begins into her disappearance, those who met Sadie cannot forget their encounters with her. <br /><br />Sadie’s story is split between Sadie’s narrative and a podcast about her disappearance. While this could have felt gimmicky, the split between the two narratives is handled with finesse. The podcast provides a different insight into Sadie’s character, and the juxtaposition between the two is fascinating. <br /><br /><b>This is not a pretty read. </b> Sadie’s raw pain emanates from the pages. There were times when I had to set this book aside because I couldn't endure reading any more of her story. I was constantly worried about her and wanted to jump into this book and rescue her on many occasions. <br /><br />This was a jarring and sometimes uncomfortable read. However, it was extremely impactful. Summer’s brings Sadie’s character to life, and while this wasn’t always enjoyable to read, her style is enthralling. <b> I was captivated by Sadie’s voice; she got under my skin and shattered my heart. </b><br /><br />I highly recommend Sadie and this is by far one of my favorite reads of 2018. <br /><br />Triggers: rape, pedophilia, violence<br /><br />I received an ARC of <i>Sadie</i> from NetGalley and St. Martin’s Press in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17298512807597083976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2537970338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2537970338" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2537970338?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2537970338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8877028141324172818"><i>Edit: Had to change my rating to 5 stars. This book has lingered for a while and each time it popped into my head, I think about how impactful it was to read a story like this.</i><br/><br/>Well, I wasn’t expecting for this story to creep up on me the way it did. <br/><br/>I think it’s best to go on not knowing what the plot of the story is about, but I will try and articulate what it encompassed and how it made me feel. <br/><br/>More than anything I feel like this is a love story. A love story gone wrong. It’s a heartbreaking </span>
  <span id="freeText8877028141324172818" style="display:none"><i>Edit: Had to change my rating to 5 stars. This book has lingered for a while and each time it popped into my head, I think about how impactful it was to read a story like this.</i><br /><br />Well, I wasn’t expecting for this story to creep up on me the way it did. <br /><br />I think it’s best to go on not knowing what the plot of the story is about, but I will try and articulate what it encompassed and how it made me feel. <br /><br />More than anything I feel like this is a love story. A love story gone wrong. It’s a heartbreaking tale on what being deprived of love can do to one’s soul. I don’t know if at any point I could pinpoint who to blame for the tragedy. And when I say love story, I’m talking familial in this case. It’s a story about what love can drive us to do and not do. The different forms it takes, what it can translate into and that the reality of it is that at times, it can be downright ugly. <br /><br />I wasn’t sure what to expect going in. The pacing was a bit too slow at the beginning but as the story began to unravel and more meat was added on, and the two different formats the story was told in began to collide, I became more and more invested and the tragedy of it all started to seep in to me. These were a bunch of characters dealing as well as they could’ve with the cards that they had been dealt with. Decisions were made for better and for worse and the consequences of their actions propelled their fates forward. <br /><br />I appreciated the ending. I think it was the right ending for this type of story. It was real and raw and reminded me that endings do not need to be tied up or have to be something conclusive. Yes, we look for something out of this realm at times when we read and we want answers, because so much of it might be missing from our lives. But this ending fitted the story well. Fits our world well. It’s haunting and it definitely has left its mark on me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8877028141324172818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10624464108578936058" style="display:none">I read this book in the least cool way to read it, and it was still unbelievably cool. I did not deserve coolness, and yet I received it. <br><br>To anyone who lives under a rock that is impenetrable to news of Cool Things: First, may I suggest you move? Sounds like a terrible place to live. Under a rock that is specifically uncool. Anyway, due to the direness of your living situation, you would not have heard of this book, and so it is my solemn duty to tell you that this book is half podcast. The chapters alternate between the story of our main character, Sadie, who is on a mission to avenge her little sister’s death, and a podcast chronicling what happened to Sadie after she left home.<br><br>And they actually RECORDED THE PODCAST. As if it were a real true crime thing. <br><br>This book can therefore be consumed in three ways:<br>1) as an audiobook, which includes the podcast<br>2) by reading the Sadie chapters and listening to the podcast chapters as the podcast<br>3) by reading the whole thing<br><br>I, a fool, just wanted to binge read this book. So I read the ebook in a day.<br><br>I regret my choices. And yet this experience was still f*cking rad, because this book is super good.<br><br>To be honest, the thing about this that was specifically exciting to me was the true crime bit. I love true crime, but I do not often consume it because I HATE stories without endings. I hate problems without solutions. I do not deal well with the Unsolved, which is about 99% of true crime.<br><br>This is why fictional narratives that mimic true crime, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555916573?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Truly Devious</a>, are perfect for me. Stories I like without the brain-breaking part!<br><br><br>Unfortunately, this usually felt more like Dark Sad Contemporary than True Crime. And while I do love contemporaries, I like Fun Fluffy ones with Friendship and Banter and sometimes a Romance. Usually set in the Summer, on a Cute Local Beach. You know?<br><br>This is the opposite of that.<br><br>But even with all of that overwhelming disappointment, this book was still good.<br><br>I guess the point of this review is there is really no reason I should have liked this book, and yet I truly did. So you should read it.<br><br>Bottom line: By my standards, this is a raving recommendation.<br><br>-----<br><i>pre-review</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495817053ra/22858671.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>should i have done it? questionable.<br><br>review to come<br><br>-----<br><br>me: (has class basically from 2 pm to 10 pm)<br><br>also me: i want to binge read Sadie today. I'M GOING TO BINGE READ SADIE TODAY</span>
  <a data-text-id="10624464108578936058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2662127429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3336796028771799287">The word <i>riveting</i> doesn't even begin to describe this masterwork by Courtney Summers. The opening pages are unassuming, but Summers soon hooks her audience with a death grip and doesn't let go. <br/><br/>The magnetism of <i>Sadie</i> is not limited to the depth and despair of its subject matter (which will remain unnamed so that new readers can pick up this book, as I did, knowing little about it and therefore be swept away fully and completely - *see note below for trigger warnings). The topics explored tickle </span>
  <span id="freeText3336796028771799287" style="display:none">The word <i>riveting</i> doesn't even begin to describe this masterwork by Courtney Summers. The opening pages are unassuming, but Summers soon hooks her audience with a death grip and doesn't let go. <br /><br />The magnetism of <i>Sadie</i> is not limited to the depth and despair of its subject matter (which will remain unnamed so that new readers can pick up this book, as I did, knowing little about it and therefore be swept away fully and completely - *see note below for trigger warnings). The topics explored tickle one's sense of grim curiosity and stir unease in one's gut. <br /><br />Nineteen-year-old Sadie is, herself, an enormous draw. She delivers her version of the story in a first-person voice that is uniquely her own. She is fierce and indomitable, facing her demons head-on, yet there's a softness to her, a yearning, and simple struggles that make her feel human and flawed. She materializes fully on the page, and rooting for her is inevitable, despite her dark motives.<br /><br />The brilliance of <i>Sadie</i> is its rawness, its unflinching examination of truth, and the masterful way Summers toys with her audience. She is the spider, and we are the fly falling victim to her web of manipulation. (Each moment of subtle weaving earned a soft gasp from this enraptured reader.) <br /><br />Harrowing, addicting, and utterly devastating, <i>Sadie</i> leaves a wound that may never heal.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>My body is sharp enough to cut glass and in desperate need of rounding out, but sometimes I don't mind. A body might not always be beautiful, but a body can be a beautiful deception. I'm stronger than I look.</i>
</blockquote><br />-<br />* Trigger Warning: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This book concerns the murder of young girls, pedophilia, substance abuse, and sexual assault/rape. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_2426384325" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2426384325" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family-drama">family-drama</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2426384325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15839258109004438944">Sadie’s sister—the light of her life—was taken from her, murdered. <br/><br/>Now, Sadie is out for blood. She’s going to find Mattie’s murderer, whatever the cost. She won’t stop at anything until she holds the heart of the bastard who destroyed Sadie’s reason to live in her hands and plunges a knife right into it. <br/><br/>I loved Sadie.<br/><br/>This may seem like a shocking statement, but Sadie is a good person. She may have dark thoughts and an even darker past, but deep down she is a human being who suffers 24/7. She d</span>
  <span id="freeText15839258109004438944" style="display:none">Sadie’s sister—the light of her life—was taken from her, murdered. <br /><br />Now, Sadie is out for blood. She’s going to find Mattie’s murderer, whatever the cost. She won’t stop at anything until she holds the heart of the bastard who destroyed Sadie’s reason to live in her hands and plunges a knife right into it. <br /><br />I loved Sadie.<br /><br />This may seem like a shocking statement, but Sadie is a good person. She may have dark thoughts and an even darker past, but deep down she is a human being who suffers 24/7. She didn’t ask to be abused. She didn’t ask to grow up faster than imaginable. <br /><br />Courtney Summers is an author who isn’t afraid to tackle heavy issues. She’s a hit or miss—BECAUSE of how audacious she is—but there isn’t a book from her that left me completely or partly indifferent. She’s not someone I can shrug off. Her words reach the deepest parts of me.<br /><br />It’s terrifying. Reading her, that is. I can never know if I’m going to cry, feel helpless, scared or overjoyed. I wouldn’t bet on the last one if I were you. Chances are, when I finish one of her books, I will slowly go to a quiet corner of my room, drop on my knees, and let all the salty water fall from my eyes.<br /><br />The only part of this book that made me narrow my eyes in incomprehension was the ending. I’m not exactly *surprised* the author did this to us, and part of me—the reasonable one—wants to argue that it’s a realistic last chapter, but I am not satisfied. I like concrete answers. Too much in a human being’s life is unsure, so I am expecting book endings to at least give me what I want.<br /><br />But that’s not a reason not to pick up this book, especially since it deserves to be read and Sadie will feel as realistic to you as the—what’s deeply twisted?—Twizzlers you just ate. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2828579586" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5187820287305793241">3.35/5 ⭐<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597073933i/29944336._SY540_.jpg' width='260' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I bought <i>
  <b>Sadie</b>
</i> so long ago I don't even remember when. I do remember that I was kind of excited to get it. But I think I bought this so long ago that my enthusiasm vanished.<br/><br/><b>It wasn't a bad book.</b><br/><br/>I really found it interesting that it was written in this podcast-interview style, even though sometimes it took me a bit too long to wrap my head around the story.<br/><br/>The reality of the book is terrible, brutal and cruel and it pains me to think that things like that happen to children in real li</span>
  <span id="freeText5187820287305793241" style="display:none">3.35/5 ⭐<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597073933i/29944336._SY540_.jpg" width="260" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I bought <i>
  <b>Sadie</b>
</i> so long ago I don't even remember when. I do remember that I was kind of excited to get it. But I think I bought this so long ago that my enthusiasm vanished.<br><br><b>It wasn't a bad book.</b><br><br>I really found it interesting that it was written in this podcast-interview style, even though sometimes it took me a bit too long to wrap my head around the story.<br><br>The reality of the book is terrible, brutal and cruel and it pains me to think that things like that happen to children in real life. No child should be treated the way Sadie has been treated. By life, mostly. I felt the pain and the anger of this girl. I really did.<br><br>But, the truth is, this book was just all right. It was a thriller-type in its own right and I appreciated the story, but it did not impress me the way it should have. And the fact that I've been "left in a tree" as we say in Romanian is not a forte of the book. <br><br>I wanted to know what exactly happened with Sadie by the end, but that final detail never came. So I was left wondering. <br>Not cool.<br><br>This is definitely a good book with a crushing story that mirrors some people's reality, but somehow it did not get to me the way I hoped it would.</span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('v/HBw8ap7kUDM99EDE6Tzyf9seX7x8PihEM37AEkkYIgP9XVXq4vSasplpv3DHVh80jzwO7dPYysQZYaJkKGkQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lkXgj4WLZMggVY8/Aanm/bZKpQ7+wCAM98LWY08nzJ8Ji/SZHYylxIhPxuD66wBTYv/nK+va3mLfwHeVaEHbjA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

It was founded by Albert Ellingham, an early twentieth century tycoon, who wanted to make a wonderful place full of riddles, twisting pathways<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2947101512963406958\" style=\"display:none\">Ellingham Academy is a famous private school in Vermont for the brightest thinkers, inventors, and artists. It was founded by Albert Ellingham, an early twentieth century tycoon, who wanted to make a wonderful place full of riddles, twisting pathways, and gardens. “A place,” he said, “where learning is a game.”\n\nShortly after the school opened, his wife and daughter were kidnapped. The only real clue was a mocking riddle listing methods of murder, signed with the frightening pseudonym “Truly, Devious.” It became one of the great unsolved crimes of American history.\n\nTrue-crime aficionado Stevie Bell is set to begin her first year at Ellingham Academy, and she has an ambitious plan: She will solve this cold case. That is, she will solve the case when she gets a grip on her demanding new school life and her housemates: the inventor, the novelist, the actor, the artist, and the jokester. But something strange is happening. Truly Devious makes a surprise return, and death revisits Ellingham Academy. The past has crawled out of its grave. Someone has gotten away with murder. \n\nThe two interwoven mysteries of this first book in the Truly Devious series dovetail brilliantly, and Stevie Bell will continue her relentless quest for the murderers in books two and three.\n\nNew York Times bestselling author Maureen Johnson weaves a delicate tale of murder and mystery in the first book of a striking new series, perfect for fans of Agatha Christie and E. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14167898933901347687">Courtney Summers is the bestselling author of several novels, whose career in writing began in 2008, when she was 22. Her work has been released to critical acclaim and multiple starred reviews, received numerous awards and honors including the Edgar Award, the John Spray Mystery Award, the Cybils Award, the Odyssey Award, the Audie Award, and has enjoyed the recognition of many library, state, 'B</span>
  <span id="freeText14167898933901347687" style="display:none">Courtney Summers is the bestselling author of several novels, whose career in writing began in 2008, when she was 22. Her work has been released to critical acclaim and multiple starred reviews, received numerous awards and honors including the Edgar Award, the John Spray Mystery Award, the Cybils Award, the Odyssey Award, the Audie Award, and has enjoyed the recognition of many library, state, 'Best Of' and Readers' Choice lists. Courtney has reviewed for The <em>New York Times</em>, is the founder of #ToTheGirls, a 2015 worldwide trending hashtag, and in 2016, she was named one of <em>Flare</em> Magazine's 60 under 30. She lives and writes in Canada. Her new novel, <em>The Project</em> releases February 2nd, 2021 from Wednesday Books, an imprint of St. Martin's Press. You can follow her on <a href="http://instagram.com/summerscourtney" target="ig" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>, <a href="http://twitter.com/courtney_s" target="twitter" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/CourtneySummersAuthor/" target="fb" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>.</span>
